37:1196:110535:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:additional $6.7 million (2012 dollars) awarded as 4,800 scholarships per year. Scholarship values may not
37:1197:110640:20:45:72:495:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:exceed the actual amount of tuition charged, or the amount charged to non-scholarship students.
37:1198:110735:45:33:72:476:645:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:Appendix B: Description of Data (for online publication)
37:1199:110791:33:27:72:223:612:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Enrollment and Tax Data
37:1200:110814:27:20:72:540:585:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The financial data we use come primarily from the Core Financial Files produced by the National Center for
37:1201:110920:20:20:72:540:565:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Charitable Statistics (NCCS) from the Internal Revenue Service’s (IRS) Return Transaction Files. These
37:1202:111022:20:20:72:540:545:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:files contain financial information collected from Internal Revenue Service Form 990 and Form 990-EZ for
37:1203:111126:20:19:72:539:525:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:501(c)(3) public charities with at least $25,000 in gross receipts.47Many religiously affiliated organizations,
37:1204:111237:19:20:72:540:506:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:such as Catholic schools, are not required to file Form 990 or Form 990-EZ and are not included in these
37:1205:111341:20:20:72:102:486:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f5:B:data.48
37:1206:111348:20:20:86:539:466:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:There are two notions of “year” to consider in the Core Files. The first is the fiscal year reported on a tax
37:1207:111457:20:20:71:539:446:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:return; this is the notion of a year that is most relevant for our study. The second is the “circa year,” which
37:1208:111568:20:20:71:539:426:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:refers to the year that a particular set of tax returns was assembled by the NCCS for inclusion in the Core
37:1209:111675:20:20:71:539:406:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:data files. The NCCS creates its “circa year” data files at the beginning of each year by collecting financial
37:1210:111785:20:20:71:540:386:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:information from the most recent available tax return for each organization.49We combine these files for
37:1211:111889:20:20:72:540:366:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:1989-2010 to create our sample. The term “circa year” thus refers to the year that a set of tax returns was
37:1212:111996:20:20:72:540:346:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:collected. This may not be the same as the fiscal year since, when the NCCS collects its data and assembles
37:1213:112103:20:20:72:540:326:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:a “circa year” dataset, the most recent available tax record for a nonprofit may not be from the most recent
37:1214:112211:20:20:72:540:306:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:fiscal year, and an organization may thus have the same fiscal year record appear in multiple circa years.
37:1215:112317:20:20:72:540:286:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:In these cases, we keep the record from the most recent circa year and drop older records of the duplicated
37:1216:112424:20:20:72:540:266:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:fiscal year. We match the tax-return data to other datasets using the fiscal year reported on the tax return,
37:1217:112533:20:20:72:187:246:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:rather than the circa year.
37:1218:112560:20:19:86:539:226:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Our primary financial variable of interest is “program service revenue.”  Reported in Part VIII, line
37:1219:112661:19:20:72:540:207:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:2g of the 2012 version of Form 990, program service revenue is income a non-profit organization generates
37:1220:112766:20:20:72:539:187:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:by charging for the provision of its tax-exempt service.50Private school tuition is a canonical example of
37:1221:112872:20:15:72:540:167:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:program service revenue, but this variable could also include revenue derived from other sources, such as the
37:1222:112981:15:10:79:374:152:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:47Beginning in tax year 2010, the filing threshold was $50,000 in gross receipts.
37:1223:113062:10:12:79:540:142:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:48Although the information on these forms is collected for tax compliance purposes, researchers have concluded that error
37:1224:113183:12:7:72:372:130:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:rates are suitably low for use in academic research. See Pollak and Pettit (1998).
37:1225:113265:7:12:79:540:123:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:49More specifically, a circa year file will include all the returns received by the IRS in a certain calendar year as well as returns
37:1226:113398:12:9:72:540:111:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:of organizations that have filed in the previous two years but do not appear in the present year’s files. In more recent years,
37:1227:113525:9:10:72:540:102:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:NCCS has started creating files that are organized by fiscal year rather than circa year. However, these fiscal year files are not
37:1228:113655:10:9:72:86:92:8:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f6:F:available for the period of our study.50
37:1229:113695:9:10:87:540:83:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:The previous version of Form 990 reported program service revenue in Section I, Line 2. Form 990-EZ also reports program
37:1230:113815:10:0:72:506:73:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:service revenue in Section I, Line 2. The definition of program service revenue does not change across years or forms.
38:1231:113935:0:20:72:308:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:provision of food service or the sale of school supplies.
38:1232:113992:20:20:86:539:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:For data on enrollment and other school characteristics, we use the Private School Universe Survey (PSS).
38:1233:114097:20:20:72:540:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Conducted biennially by the National Center for Education Statistics (NCES), the PSS is meant to be a
38:1234:114198:20:20:72:540:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:census of private schools in the United States. Response rates are routinely in excess of 90%. The survey
38:1235:114303:20:20:72:540:630:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:covers enrollment, grades offered, number of teachers, religious affiliation, and racial composition, but it does
38:1236:114416:20:20:72:540:610:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:not include any financial information about schools. We next describe the procedure of matching these two
38:1237:114521:20:37:72:110:590:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:datasets.
38:1238:114530:37:27:72:352:553:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Crosswalk and School Identification Procedures
38:1239:114576:27:20:72:540:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:In order to create a dataset that contains financial and enrollment information for the same schools, we
38:1240:114680:20:19:72:540:506:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:create a crosswalk between the NCCS data and the PSS. Although the two datasets do not contain a
38:1241:114776:19:20:72:540:487:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:common identifier, the PSS data contain schools’ names beginning in 2005-06 and schools’ street addresses
38:1242:114881:20:20:72:540:467:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:beginning in 2007-08. The NCCS data contain names and addresses in all years. Using all years of NCCS
38:1243:114982:20:20:72:540:447:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:data and the 2005-06, 2007-08, and 2009-10 rounds of the PSS, we match names and addresses to create
38:1244:115082:20:20:72:540:427:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:a crosswalk between the two datasets that links an organization’s Employer Identification Number (EIN),
38:1245:115185:20:20:72:540:407:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:reported on its tax forms, to its NCES-assigned PIN number. We then use this EIN-PIN correspondence to
38:1246:115287:20:20:72:348:387:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:match tax and enrollment records in all available years of data.
38:1247:115351:20:20:86:539:367:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:In constructing our crosswalk, we collect four types of matches: exact address matches (street address,
38:1248:115454:20:20:72:540:347:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:zip code and state), exact name matches within the same zip code, similar names within “zip plus four” area,
38:1249:115562:20:20:72:540:327:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and exact name matches within the same state, allowing for zip code mismatches. Address-based matches
38:1250:115663:20:20:72:540:307:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in the last two cases were inspected and names compared manually to ensure accuracy.  This procedure
38:1251:115763:20:20:72:540:287:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:generates a small number of cases in which we match a single EIN to multiple PINs or vice versa.  We
38:1252:115863:20:20:72:188:267:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f5:B:discard all such matches.51
38:1253:115890:20:20:86:539:247:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:In addition to those matched using our crosswalk, we identify schools in the NCCS data using their
38:1254:115988:20:19:71:539:227:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:National Taxonomy of Exempt Entities (NTEE) Classification System codes, which the IRS uses to classify
38:1255:116091:19:20:71:539:208:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:non-profit organizations. We consider schools that are classified using codes B20 (elementary and secondary
38:1256:116198:20:20:71:539:188:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:schools), B24 (primary and elementary schools), and B25 (secondary and high schools). We do not consider
38:1257:116302:20:20:71:539:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:preschools (code B21), since the scholarships financed by the tax credits we study generally cannot be used
38:1258:116409:20:20:71:539:148:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to attend preschool. This approach also does not identify any organizations that function as schools but are
38:1259:116517:20:15:71:539:128:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:identified using other codes. A Christian high school, for example might be identified by NTEE code X20,
38:1260:116621:15:12:79:540:113:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:51One could imagine cases in which one identifier or the other might change for legitimate reasons (e.g. a school could come
38:1261:116745:12:10:72:540:101:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:under new management, or it could reincorporate itself as a tax entity, leading a single PIN to match, appropriately, to multiple
38:1262:116874:10:9:72:540:91:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:EINs, or a single non-profit organization operates multiple schools, leading a single EIN to match to multiple PINs). However,
38:1263:117000:9:10:72:540:82:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:the EIN in the NCCS data and the PIN in the PSS are generally intended to be permanent identifiers, so in most cases they
38:1264:117121:10:0:72:179:72:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:should not change over time.
39:1265:117151:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:a code used for organizations related to Christianity, instead of B25. Similarly, a school for developmentally
39:1266:117261:20:20:72:540:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:disabled children might be classified using code P82 (developmentally disabled centers) rather than one of
39:1267:117367:20:20:72:540:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the codes we consider. Since organizations are only classified using one NTEE code, we are unable to identify
39:1268:117476:20:37:72:311:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:any schools that are not classified primarily as schools.
39:1269:117533:37:26:72:364:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Differences between Enrollment and Tax Samples
39:1270:117579:26:20:72:540:587:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The PSS and NCCS data are collected with very different goals, and so there are important differences
39:1271:117680:20:20:72:540:567:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:between the types of schools found in each sample. The PSS is intended to include all schools that offer
39:1272:117784:20:20:72:540:547:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:classroom instruction in at least one grade from kindergarten through twelfth grade and are not supported
39:1273:117889:20:20:72:540:527:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:by public money. There are no enrollment, revenue, or religious affiliation requirements for inclusion in the
39:1274:117998:20:20:72:482:507:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f5:B:PSS. Since charter schools are supported by public money, they are not covered by the PSS.52
39:1275:118090:20:20:86:539:487:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:The NCCS data describe non-profit organizations generally and only incidentally include schools. More-
39:1276:118192:20:20:71:539:467:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:over, since filing requirements are designed to apply generally, broad categories of schools are likely to be
39:1277:118301:20:20:71:539:447:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:under-represented in the NCCS data. Most notably, many religious organizations are not required to pay
39:1278:118403:20:20:71:539:427:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:taxes, file tax returns, or even register with the IRS. Many religious organizations also operate private schools.
39:1279:118517:20:20:71:539:407:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Schools operated by religious organizations, therefore, are less likely to be included in the NCCS data than
39:1280:118625:20:20:71:539:387:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:they are to be included in the PSS, which surveys schools of all religious affiliations. The NCCS data may
39:1281:118731:20:20:71:539:367:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:also miss small schools with very low levels of revenue, since organizations with gross receipts under $25,000
39:1282:118841:20:20:71:539:347:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:during our analysis period were not required to file Form 990 or Form 990-EZ. The vast majority of schools
39:1283:118947:20:19:71:539:327:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:are likely exceed this threshold, but a small, kindergarten-terminal school, for example, could conceivably
39:1284:119054:19:20:71:539:308:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:fall below the revenue cutoff for inclusion in the NCCS data while still appearing in the PSS, since it offers
39:1285:119164:20:20:71:129:288:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:kindergarten.
39:1286:119177:20:20:86:539:268:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:These differences between the PSS and NCCS data also imply that the set of schools we are able to
39:1287:119274:20:20:71:539:248:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:match to a tax record will differ from the set of schools we are not able to match. Across all years, matched
39:1288:119383:20:20:71:539:228:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:schools have higher enrollment (both including and excluding preschool) and employ more teachers than
39:1289:119484:20:20:71:539:208:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:unmatched schools. A substantially smaller share of matched schools are affiliated with the Catholic church,
39:1290:119592:20:20:71:539:188:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:and a substantially larger share are nonsectarian. Matched schools have slightly lower rates of affiliation
39:1291:119699:20:20:71:539:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:with religions other than Catholicism. Appendix Figure 2 plots the share of matched and unmatched schools
39:1292:119804:20:20:71:539:148:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:that are religious (Catholic or not) or non religious. (Trends for total enrollment and total teachers are given
39:1293:119916:20:20:71:539:128:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in Figure 3 in the main text.) Although the levels differ, trends are similar across the two groups. These
39:1294:120022:20:20:71:539:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:pictures look roughly the same if we produce them using all years of PSS data for schools in our crosswalk
39:1295:120128:20:14:71:362:88:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:instead of just those years in which we match them to tax records.
39:1296:120194:14:0:79:506:74:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:52Charter schools are included in the Common Core of Data, the survey of public schools conducted by the NCES.
40:1297:120306:0:20:86:539:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix Table 1 reports school counts and enrollment totals for the full PSS, crosswalk, and matched
40:1298:120407:20:20:72:540:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:samples.  As one would expect based on the procedure used to create our crosswalk, the crosswalk and
40:1299:120507:20:20:72:540:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:matched samples include a larger share of total schools and total students in more recent years, with the
40:1300:120612:20:37:72:473:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:matched sample including more than 20% of all students in 2005 and reaching 25% in 2009.
40:1301:120700:37:27:72:381:613:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Who files Form 990?  Why is our match rate so low?
40:1302:120750:27:20:72:540:586:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Failures to match PSS records with tax data are generally due to the absence of a school’s return from
40:1303:120852:20:20:72:540:566:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the tax data or the limited nature of the information available for identifying matches. Tax returns may
40:1304:120956:20:20:72:540:546:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:be unavailable for a variety of reasons. Although Catholic schools probably constitute the most significant
40:1305:121063:20:20:72:540:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:group generally exempt from the requirement to file Form 990 for religious reasons, other religious schools
40:1306:121170:20:19:72:540:506:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:may qualify for the exemption as well. In each year of the PSS, at least two thirds (and up to 84%) of schools
40:1307:121280:19:20:72:540:487:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:report having a religious orientation or purpose, and at least half of those religious schools are non-Catholic.
40:1308:121392:20:20:72:540:467:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Religious exemption from the requirement to file Form 990 requires a school to be affiliated with a church or
40:1309:121501:20:20:72:540:447:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:religious order, so religiously oriented schools without such an affiliation can and do appear in our tax data,
40:1310:121612:20:20:72:540:427:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:but there is clearly substantial scope for schools not to appear in the tax data due to religious exemption
40:1311:121719:20:20:72:540:407:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from the filing requirement. A school’s return could also fail to appear in the tax data if it typically has
40:1312:121827:20:20:72:540:387:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:gross receipts under $25,000, if it is operated by an organization that files taxes under a section of the
40:1313:121933:20:20:72:540:367:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Internal Revenue Code other than 501(c)(3), or if it is negligent in its responsibility to file, though taken
40:1314:122042:20:20:72:540:347:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:individually each of these are likely less important factors than the religious exemption. The limited nature
40:1315:122151:20:20:72:540:327:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of the information available for identifying matches likely also leads to failures to match records from the
40:1316:122259:20:20:72:540:307:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:PSS to the tax data. Our matches are based on school names and addresses. At the time we matched these
40:1317:122361:20:20:72:540:287:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:records, school names were only available in the PSS in three years, and school addresses were available
40:1318:122465:20:20:72:540:267:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:in only two.  Although we processed and checked the data thoroughly to identify matches, the inherent
40:1319:122566:20:20:72:540:247:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:variability in how different people write information like this on forms may have lead to some failures to
40:1320:122672:20:19:72:540:227:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:match. Even in some cases in which a school’s name and address are recorded correctly, we are unable to
40:1321:122775:19:20:72:540:208:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:match it to a tax record if the organization that operates it (and files its tax return) does not share its name
40:1322:122887:20:20:72:119:188:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:or address.
40:1323:122898:20:20:86:539:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix Table 2 gives information on our matching success across states for different types of school.
40:1324:123001:20:20:72:540:148:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The first column is the average number of private schools observed in a round of the PSS in a state. The
40:1325:123105:20:20:72:540:128:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:next column, “crosswalked” observations, gives the average number of schools in a round of the PSS that we
40:1326:123211:20:20:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:are able to match to the tax data in any year (i.e. the number of schools from our PSS-tax data crosswalk
40:1327:123316:20:0:72:540:88:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:that appear in the PSS in an average year). The “cross walk %” column reports column 2 over column 1:
41:1328:123419:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the average percent of schools in a wave of the PSS that we observe in our tax data. Focusing on this percent
41:1329:123528:20:20:72:540:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:column, most match rates are around 20% to 25%; the worst is Wisconsin, and the best is Vermont. Our
41:1330:123628:20:20:72:540:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:treatment states appear fairly close to other states, with Pennsylvania the lowest. Looking at the middle set
41:1331:123737:20:20:72:540:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of columns, our success in matching Catholic schools is (unsurprisingly) poor, with a success rate of 5 to 10
41:1332:123846:20:20:72:540:630:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:percent for most states. Again, the treatment states’ matching rates are not remarkably different, although
41:1333:123953:20:20:72:540:610:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Pennsylvania is again the least matched. The matching rate for other religious schools is higher, but still
41:1334:124060:20:20:72:540:590:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:somewhat small, with typically about the same match rate as for the overall sample. Among the treatment
41:1335:124163:20:20:72:540:570:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:states, Pennsylvania is lowest while Iowa is somewhat higher than most observations (a 36% matching rate
41:1336:124267:20:20:72:540:550:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:versus a 20-25% rate for most observations), but this notwithstanding, the overall collection of treatment
41:1337:124373:20:20:72:540:530:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:states is again similar to the controls in matching success. Lastly, for nonsectarian schools, the matching
41:1338:124480:20:20:72:540:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:rate is somewhat higher, about 40%, while the treatment states are slightly lower than the average with
41:1339:124583:20:20:72:540:490:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:most having match rates around 30%. Overall, as expected we do a better job (but still far from perfect)
41:1340:124687:20:20:72:540:470:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:matching nonsectarian schools than religious schools, and our treatment states have matching rates that
41:1341:124790:20:37:72:344:450:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:appear reasonably close to what is seen for the overall sample.
41:1342:124853:37:26:72:316:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Standardizing Fiscal and Academic Years
41:1343:124892:26:20:72:540:387:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:The task of matching each school’s financial information to its enrollment information for the appropriate
41:1344:124998:20:20:72:540:367:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:year is complicated by the fact that many schools use fiscal years that differ from their academic years. The
41:1345:125107:20:20:72:540:347:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:PSS asks administrators to report enrollment at the beginning of October, and schools often require students
41:1346:125215:20:20:72:540:327:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:to have paid tuition at the beginning of the school year. It is important, therefore, to make sure that the
41:1347:125322:20:20:72:477:307:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:tax records we match to each enrollment record includes the beginning of the academic year.
41:1348:125413:20:20:86:539:287:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:We address this issue by assigning an academic year to each NCCS observation based on the calendar
41:1349:125511:20:20:72:540:267:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:year in which the October of its fiscal year falls. For example, suppose we observe a tax record for a school
41:1350:125620:20:20:72:540:247:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:with a July 1, 2003 – June 30, 2004 fiscal year. The October of this school’s fiscal year is in 2003, so we
41:1351:125727:20:19:72:540:227:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:assign this tax record to the 2003-04 academic year. If this school used a January 1, 2003 – December 31,
41:1352:125832:19:20:72:540:208:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:2003 fiscal year, this tax record would still be assigned to the 2003-04 academic year, because its fiscal year
41:1353:125943:20:20:72:540:188:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:contains October 2003. However, if the school instead used a November 1, 2003 – October 31, 2004 fiscal
41:1354:126046:20:20:72:376:168:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:year, this tax record would be assigned to the 2004-05 academic year.
41:1355:126115:20:20:86:539:148:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:For the schools in our data, the most commonly used fiscal year runs from July 1 through June 30, with
41:1356:126217:20:20:72:540:128:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:over 60% of tax records in each circa year following this calendar. This means that financial and enrollment
41:1357:126325:20:20:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:information align very well for most of our matched schools. There is a large drop in the number of schools
41:1358:126432:20:0:72:540:88:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:with fiscal-year 1998 tax returns in the data; this drop is driven by a decline in the number of organizations
42:1359:126544:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:with a fiscal year ending in June and is not a product of our crosswalk procedure, but rather is observed in
42:1360:126652:20:20:72:540:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the “raw” Core data. This decline appears to be driven by a change enacted in June of 1999 affecting public
42:1361:126759:20:38:72:225:670:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f5:B:disclosure of nonprofit 990 forms.53
42:1362:126795:38:26:72:133:632:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Covariates
42:1363:126805:26:20:72:540:606:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Our control variables come from a variety of sources.  We use median incomes reported by the Census
42:1364:126904:20:20:72:540:586:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Bureau and unemployment rates reported by the Bureau of Labor Statistics. For the purpose of calculating
42:1365:127008:20:20:72:540:566:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:population densities, we obtain the land area of each state from the Census Bureau’s Statistical Abstracts of
42:1366:127117:20:20:72:540:546:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the United States, 2002 edition. Population and the fraction who are noncitizens, born abroad, and in various
42:1367:127226:20:20:72:540:526:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:age-race/ethnicity groups are calculated using data obtained from IPUMS for the 1990 and 2000 censuses,
42:1368:127329:20:19:72:540:506:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:as well as the American Community Survey from 2001-2009.  We linearly interpolate to produce values
42:1369:127428:19:20:72:540:487:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of the shares of residents who are noncitizens and born abroad for 1991-1999. For the age-race/ethnicity
42:1370:127532:20:20:72:540:467:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:covariates, we produce values for 1991-1999 by assigning individuals in the 2000 census to the appropriate
42:1371:127638:20:38:72:449:447:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:state-age-race/ethnicity group for each of those years, using state of residence in 2000.
42:1372:127727:38:26:72:338:409:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Sample Restrictions for School-level Analysis
42:1373:127772:26:20:72:540:383:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:For schools with matched financial and enrollment records, we construct a measure that approximates tuition
42:1374:127879:20:20:72:540:363:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:by dividing total program service revenue by total enrollment. While we believe this to be the best available
42:1375:127988:20:20:72:540:343:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:method of estimating tuition, it does produce some figures that are implausibly large, reaching into the
42:1376:128092:20:20:72:540:323:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:hundreds of thousands and even millions of dollars. To some extent, seemingly high estimates of tuition arise
42:1377:128201:20:20:72:540:303:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:from the fact that program service revenue includes income from both tuition and other sources, but this
42:1378:128305:20:19:72:540:283:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:cannot explain tuition estimates of seven figures or more. High tuition estimates could also be a product of
42:1379:128413:19:20:72:540:264:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:matches between a school’s enrollment record and the tax return of a parent organization that also receives
42:1380:128520:20:20:72:540:244:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:substantial revenue from other sources. For example, a university could operate a kindergarten-terminal
42:1381:128623:20:20:72:540:224:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:preschool for the children of its staff. If the enrollment record of that preschool matched to the university’s
42:1382:128734:20:20:72:540:204:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:tax return, our measure of that preschool’s tuition could easily reach tens or hundreds of millions of dollars.
42:1383:128845:20:15:72:540:184:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, high tuition estimates could simply be a result of outliers in the data. The NCCS data documentation
42:1384:128954:15:12:79:540:169:6:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:F:53Beginning in June 1999, IRS regulations required all 501(c) organizations except private foundations to provide copies of
42:1385:129077:12:10:72:540:157:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:their tax forms to anyone who requested them. If this disclosure requirement caused some schools with fiscal years ending in
42:1386:129201:10:9:72:540:147:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:June 1999 (corresponding to the 1998-99 academic year) to file their tax returns late that year (that is, after NCCS collected its
42:1387:129331:9:10:72:540:138:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:Core data at the beginning of 2000) before returning to filing on schedule in subsequent years (before the beginning of 2001),
42:1388:129457:10:9:72:540:128:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:the NCCS data collection procedure could have missed these records. The most recent available tax record for these schools
42:1389:129579:9:10:72:540:119:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:at the beginning of 2000 would have corresponded to the 1997-98 academic year, and the most recent available record in 2001
42:1390:129702:10:9:72:540:109:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:would have corresponded to the 1999-2000 academic year, missing 1998-99. Since NCCS does not update a given circa year
42:1391:129820:9:9:72:540:100:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:Core file as additional records become available, our dataset constructed from those files would be missing any tax records filed
42:1392:129949:9:0:72:145:91:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:F:late in this manner.
43:1393:129971:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:repeatedly notes (and suggest correcting for) the presence of outliers. We address excessively high tuition
43:1394:130078:20:20:72:496:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:figures in our baseline estimates by excluding schools with estimated tuition of $100,000 or more.
43:1395:130176:20:20:86:539:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:We apply several other restrictions to produce our school-level analysis sample. In both the tax data and
43:1396:130281:20:20:72:540:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the PSS, we exclude schools that report being located in different states in different years, including any
43:1397:130388:20:20:72:540:630:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:that fail to report a state in any year. We also drop tax returns for schools in outlying US territories, which
43:1398:130499:20:20:72:540:610:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:we cannot match to enrollment records, since the PSS does not cover these territories. Finally, we exclude
43:1399:130605:20:45:72:428:590:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:schools that report zero or negative program service revenue on their tax returns.
43:1400:130687:45:30:72:540:545:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:Appendix C: Description of Conley-Taber Confidence Intervals (for
43:1401:130752:30:30:72:205:515:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:online publication)

43:1464:132045:20:20:86:540:123:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:As described in the text, first we estimate, using OLS on the full sample, the equationysy=βXsy+θs+

43:1466:132253:20:0:72:540:83:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:We next randomly assign the treatment states’ index values to the control states, where the assignment is
44:1467:132360:0:20:72:540:710:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:done at the state level (e.g., the index values for all years in Arizona are assigned to Alabama). After the
44:1468:132468:20:20:72:540:690:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:five true state-index profiles have randomly been assigned to five new states we regress the residuals of the
44:1469:132577:20:20:72:540:670:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:five new states on the state-index profiles, state and year dummies, and record the coefficient. The inclusion
44:1470:132687:20:20:72:539:650:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:of the state and year dummies means the estimate is done on ̃djt, rather than the within-group difference of
44:1471:132795:20:20:72:540:630:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f3:B:d, although these should be asymptotically equivalent (see equation A2 and related discussion in Conley and
44:1472:132902:20:20:72:540:610:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:Taber’s appendix). Our approach using ̃djtis conservative and produceslargerconfidence intervals than the
44:1473:133007:20:20:72:533:590:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:within-group-difference approach. We run 5,000 such regressions to estimate a distribution of coefficients.
44:1474:133114:20:20:86:540:570:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Using these 5,000 coefficients we can construct apvalue by calculating, if ˆα>0 (ˆα<0 ),p= 2×f,
44:1475:133209:20:20:72:540:550:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:wherefis the fraction of coefficients greater than (less than) our true estimate ˆα.54We can take the 97.5
44:1476:133315:20:20:72:540:530:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:percentile value from the distribution of 5,000 and subtract this from ˆα; this is the lower-bound for our 95
44:1477:133424:20:20:72:540:510:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:percent confidence interval. We can subtract the 2.5 percentile value of this distribution from ˆαto generate
44:1478:133533:20:20:72:261:490:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:the upper bound of the confidence interval.
44:1479:133576:20:20:86:540:470:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:A:Our estimatorˆΓ(w) reflects the above representation ofˆΓ(w) except that, rather than estimate the full
44:1480:133679:20:19:72:539:450:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:B:distribution ofˆΓ(w), we randomly assign the treatment variable and conduct 5,000 draws for each confidence
44:1481:133786:19:20:72:446:431:10:g_d0_f3:7:g_d0_f5:B:interval. We are thus drawing 5,000 values ofˆΓ(w) rather than the full distribution.55
